Suresh Ramasubramanian wrote:

> At 07:38 PM 7/12/2005, Sivasankar Chander wrote:
>
>> 3) Get rid of udev, hal, etc. and downgrade to a static /dev tree.
>
>
> why?  i haven't found udev to be a significant performance hog
>
> hald and dbus on the other hand .. well they aren't too bad but you 
> might have a point there

None of them are really resource hogs and these are fundamental 
advancements which you cannot really downgrade without breaking a whole 
lot of user space apps sitting on top of it.  In fact for FC5 the whole 
init system is potentially dependant on dbus

http://fedoraproject.org/wiki/FCNewInit
https://www.redhat.com/archives/fedora-devel-list/2005-June/msg01390.html


>
>> I've just got FC4 yesterday, and I'll be trying it out shortly - but
>> it is reported
>> to be significantly faster for most C++ code - that includes stuff 
>> like Qt, KDE,
>> Mozilla, Firefox, etc.
>
>
> because of gcc 4?

GCC 4 is not expected to be a big performance improvement at this point. 
The framework for optimization from Red Hat  is entirely new. see 
http://lwn.net/Articles/84888/. Taking advantage of this framework will 
be a part of the minor point releases like GCC 4.1.  FC4 improvements 
were as a result of other changes like boot code optimisation using 
programs like bootchart (http://bootchart.sf.net) along with other work 
which has happened upstream

regards
Rahul

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Tue Jul 12 20:50:30 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Tue Jul 12 20:38:52 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (OD)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0507122011360.8934-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

International Open Source Network (IOSN) is released a detailed FOSS
Localization Guide to assists people in localizing FOSS applications.
URL: http://www.iosn.net/l10n/localization-guide/ (Thanks MadhanRaj)

One Day One Command 
===================

od -- Dump files in Octal and other formats.

Summary:

'od' (Octal Dump) writes an unambiguous representation of the file in
screen. Each line of output consists of the offset in the input,
followed by groups of data from the file.

Examples:

Create a 2 lines text file to test following examples.

$ od myfile -- Dump the content and Offset in Octal format.

$ od -a myfile -- Dump the content as named char.

$ od -b myfile -- Dump the content in octal bytes.

$ od -c myfile -- Dump the content in ASCII.

$ od -h myfile -- Dump the content in Short Hex.

$ od -w6 myfile -- Set output width to 6 Bytes. Default is 16.

$ od -j6 myfile -- Skip initial 6 Bytes.

$ od -N6 myfile -- Read only 6 Bytes.

$ od -Ad myfile -- Show Offset values in decimal.

$ od -Ax myfile -- Show Offset values in Hex.

$ od -An myfile -- Don't show the Offset.

Read: man od

Bye :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

Muthiah's One Day One GTK+ Widget:
http://gtkbook.sourceforge.net/widgetaday.html

An AMD AthlonXP 1800+ with 512MB RAM,
ASUS A7V400-MX motherboard and
NVidia GeForce2/MX video card (64 MB RAM).

There's another Pentium III 450 MHz,
256MB RAM and i440BX motherboard with
onboard S3 Trio3d video card (apparently,
an IBM 300GL desktop) on which GNOME
literally crawls.

The problem is mostly with responsiveness if
the following set of applications are open in
the default GNOME desktop:
    * mozilla/firefox/opera/epiphany
    * beep-media-player/xmms
    * xchat
    * A couple of terminal windows with emacs
      and/or zsh.

The above are being managed on 8 workspaces.
They work peacefully without a snag on
window-maker/enlightenment/openbox
(with ROX-Session).

My complaint is not against FC4, but rather against
GNOME itself. KDE is somewhat more responsive than
GNOME on my machines. It is usable on an old
Pentium II 266 MHz with 128MB RAM (Compaq
Deskpro 4000 i.e.) from a knoppix live CDROM.

However, changing the default gtk theme to something
lighter (ThinIce for instance) improves the speed
of GNOME, slightly.

> See if the following command helps.
>
> gconftool-2 --type bool --set/apps/metacity/general/reduced_resources  
> true

I'll try this out.

>
> Use system-config-services or ntsysv to turn
> off services/deamons you dont use.

I generally leave most services disabled (except
perhaps syslog, network, portmap, fam and a
few others).

FC4/RH is perhaps best suited for enterprise
servers/workstations (large memory+more CPU power),
where startup time and desktop responsiveness might
not matter the most.

For low resource constraints, there are alternatives.

Message-ID: <42D3FD05.60306@redhat.com>

Ramkumar R wrote:

>I might be deviating a bit but I guess it's still within the scope of
>this thread..Does anyone know of any good links to show how effective
>the P4/AMD64 specific optimizations (
>
Are you talking about compiler flags?.  This is recurring topic in 
Fedora-devel list

http://fedora.redhat.com/docs/release-notes/fc4/#id2497259
http://www.redhat.com/archives/fedora-devel-list/2004-September/msg01068.html

Benchmarks show that performance optimization at the compiler level  
beyond this point doesnt have any significant effect on this system 
while losing out compatibility with several class of processors and 
potentially introducing subtle bugs into the system due to the way GCC 
code optimization heuristics works. If there are speed differences 
between distributions, compiler flags arent really the answer

regards
Rahul

On Tue, 12 Jul 2005 22:44:30 +0530, Rahul Sundaram <sundaram@redhat.com>  
wrote:

> Fedora isnt really targeted at any specific market. There is a lot of  
> desktop related work happeningthere too. GTK, Dbus, HAL, NetworkManager  
> and so on.

Yes. Its a step in the right direction. But I feel
there's still a long way to go before Fedora grows
up to be aesthetically pleasing desktop. I've been
more impressed with SuSE Personal Desktop, Mandriva,
SimplyMEPIS, Xandros and Ubuntu for desktop usage.
I've found it easier to introduce a newbie desktop
user onto any of the above mentioned distros than FC.

I've also found Slackware to be the best bet for
lean servers (old 486/Pentium machines with 32 MB RAM configured as a  
firewall/router). Fedora must improve
on this front too (lean resource/disk-space
requirements for minimal installation servers). There
are these old machines still lurking around with
520 MB hard disks and FC4 simply wont install on them
while Slackware 10.1 and Debian Sarge does so, without
problems.

--
Chandrashekar Babu
http://www.chandrashekar.info/

From siva.ilugc at gmail.com  Wed Jul 13 00:44:34 2005
From: siva.ilugc at gmail.com (Sivasankar Chander)

Subject: [Ilugc] Acer 5002 notebook
In-Reply-To: <20050712164342.44379.qmail@web50201.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <1121186107.24048.238298116@webmail.messagingengine.com>
	<20050712164342.44379.qmail@web50201.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <a8f99012050712121462110a3b@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/12/05, Shakthi Kannan <cyborg4k@yahoo.com> wrote:
> 
> --- Mohammed Riyaz <p_mdriyaz@fastmail.fm> wrote:
> > A friend of mine is considering getting Acer
> 
> Cheap hardware. If you just want to use it for a year
> or so, go ahead with it.
> 

Apples and Oranges - AFAIK, the Acer 5002 is the only 64-bit
notebook available in India now. No IBM Thinkpad or Dell uses an
AMD 64 CPU, so they're stuck at 32-bit for the foreseeable future.

> Instead, you can spend a little more and get a good,
> sturdy laptop that will help you in the long run.
> 
   In the long run, any piece of computer hardware will have
depreciated in value to zero due to rapid obsolescence.

> I will recommend the Thinkpads.
> 

All Thinkpads are now sourced from Lenovo - the much-vaunted
sturdiness is probably a thing of the past. The last Thinkpad which
was both sturdy and reliable was the 1996 Thinkpad 760xl, from 1996.
Present-day Thinkpad batteries seem to fail in less than a year, 
while the original battery from my 760xl is still chugging along at nearly
full capacity after 10 years.

Incidentally, I inspected an Acer 3002 (32-bit predecessor of the 5002)
closely, and the build quality was comparable to the Lenovo-built TP R50e.
In fact, the hinges were sturdier on the Acer than the Thinkpad.
My main complaint is that Acer chose an SiS chipset with UMA instead
of going with separate AGP graphics, for both the 3002 and 5002. I 
detest integrated shared-memory graphics - it rates only slightly better
than Winmodems and Rambus on a list of crappy hardware ideas foisted
by marketroids.

I think somebody should bell the cat, and at least check if Knoppix or
similar boots cleanly on the Acer 5002.

-Siva
From balajig at future.futsoft.com  Wed Jul 13 09:29:01 2005
From: balajig at future.futsoft.com (Balaji G)
Date: Wed Jul 13 09:26:56 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Fedora Core 4 A crisp Review
Message-ID: <000001c5875f$343bbbe0$5175cb0a@future.futsoft.com>

Hi People

I installed Fedora Core 4 yesterday on my machine which has 256 MB RAM and a
Celeron 1.7 Ghz Processor and i would say that its really good when compared
to Fedora Core 3 in terms of speed. Its really faster than FC3 but i faced a
problem in Fedora Core 4 with regards to Xorg. i.e. what happened was when
the X-Server is running and when i press Ctrl + Alt + F1 i just got a blank
screen and i was unable to access any of the terminals from F1-F6 and then i
tried searching it in Bugzilla and came to know that its a known bug so i
had to replace the file libvgahw.a with FC3's libvgahw.a and the problem got
solved.

People who are facing this problem could check out this
https://bugzilla.redhat.com/bugzilla/show_bug.cgi?id=161242


Other than this i would say Fedora Core 4 is a real good distro..


HTH
Regards
Balaji

> My main complaint is that Acer chose an SiS chipset with UMA instead
> of going with separate AGP graphics, for both the 3002 and 5002. I
> detest integrated shared-memory graphics - it rates only slightly better
> than Winmodems and Rambus on a list of crappy hardware ideas foisted
> by marketroids.

Almost every notebook available in India comes with integrated
graphics with shared mem with very few exceptions. Of the Acer models
TM4002WLCi and TM4601WLMi come with discrete AGP (ATI Mobility Radeon
X700 with 64MB RAM).  They cost 65K and 72K respectively including a
copy of Win XP Pro. I wrote to Acer and got a response saying TM4601
is also available with Linux OS. Am waiting for the dealer to send me
the price of this. In other brands any model with a discrete AGP is
abv 1 lakh.

Interestingly, another Acer model, Aspire 5500 series (with abv
mentioned graphics card) and almost similar config is available in
Thailand for 50K INR (linux OS)! Considering that it costs just 14K
for a return ticket to Bangkok one can get a notebook and a holiday in
Bangkok for the same price :-)

mano
From bhuvaneswaran at gmail.com  Wed Jul 13 11:10:13 2005
From: bhuvaneswaran at gmail.com (Bhuvaneswaran A)
Date: Wed Jul 13 11:10:30 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] samba file save problem
In-Reply-To: <bc3fff52050712210924c8bc47@mail.gmail.com>
References: <bc3fff52050712210924c8bc47@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <4dc6c90405071222404e747c5c@mail.gmail.com>

>  In server the files have rwxrw-r-- permission
> on client ( mounted) files have the rw-r--r-- permission

You should permit the samba client to edit the file. You can configure
it in /etc/samba/smb.conf. You should set 'writable = yes' or
something alike. Dig into it for further details.

Regards,
Bhuvaneswaran A

S.Ramaswamy wrote:

>It was reportedly very commercial and sometimes crassly so. Not sure
>about reports that some of the speakers were led to the stage by girls
>- was it Linux Asia or some other event ?
>
Well, as far as I know, it never happened. Must be LinuxAsia, because 
they're the ones who charge mega-bucks to attend some specialized tracks 
(like sysadmin tracks et al) so they can afford to add that glitter. 
Speakers at Linux-Bangalore bring their own laptops and whatever 
material they need. Only the net connectivity, projector & hall are 
provided by the organizers. They have a pretty strict talk-proposal 
screening system.

Linux-Bangalore is not permitted to be commercial and deliberately so - 
the sponsor/vendor stalls at the event are forbidden from selling 
anything because it attracts commercial tax and lot of hassles for the 
organizers. All hand-outs are free (CDs, stickers, t-shirts, etc). And, 
I can assure you that there are very, very few girls ;-) That too, when 
some company sends in its whole workforce in a bus or something.

> The last time I attended
>BangLinux was in 2000 and it was pretty good then. Delhi is a bit far
>from Thiruvanmiyur, you know ;-)
>
>  
>
BangLinux was a sponsored event - by Wrox Publishers, if I'm not wrong. 
It no longer exists. Linux-Bangalore is a different event, conducted by 
the Bangalore Linux community. Sorry if I sound like some canvasser for 
the event, but this is one of the few decent events we have, and we 
cannot let it die due to apathy from the community. Apart from some 
minor goof-ups (like late handing of delegate kits) it's a pretty 
well-organized,  enjoyable event (hey, you get a free t-shirt too!).

Vamsee.

"History is more or less bunk" - Henry Ford

Message: 1
Date: Wed, 13 Jul 2005 00:44:34 +0530
From: Sivasankar Chander <siva.ilugc@gmail.com>
Subject: Re: [Ilugc] Acer 5002 notebook
To: ilugc@ae.iitm.ac.in
Message-ID: <a8f99012050712121462110a3b@mail.gmail.com>
Content-Type: text/plain; charset=ISO-8859-1

On 7/12/05, Shakthi Kannan <cyborg4k@yahoo.com> wrote:
> 
> --- Mohammed Riyaz <p_mdriyaz@fastmail.fm> wrote:
> > A friend of mine is considering getting Acer
> 
> Cheap hardware. If you just want to use it for a year
> or so, go ahead with it.
> 

Apples and Oranges - AFAIK, the Acer 5002 is the only 64-bit
notebook available in India now. No IBM Thinkpad or Dell uses an
AMD 64 CPU, so they're stuck at 32-bit for the foreseeable future.

> Instead, you can spend a little more and get a good,
> sturdy laptop that will help you in the long run.
> 
   In the long run, any piece of computer hardware will have
depreciated in value to zero due to rapid obsolescence.

> I will recommend the Thinkpads.
> 

All Thinkpads are now sourced from Lenovo - the much-vaunted
sturdiness is probably a thing of the past. The last Thinkpad which
was both sturdy and reliable was the 1996 Thinkpad 760xl, from 1996.
Present-day Thinkpad batteries seem to fail in less than a year, 
while the original battery from my 760xl is still chugging along at nearly
full capacity after 10 years.

Incidentally, I inspected an Acer 3002 (32-bit predecessor of the 5002)
closely, and the build quality was comparable to the Lenovo-built TP R50e.
In fact, the hinges were sturdier on the Acer than the Thinkpad.
My main complaint is that Acer chose an SiS chipset with UMA instead
of going with separate AGP graphics, for both the 3002 and 5002. I 
detest integrated shared-memory graphics - it rates only slightly better
than Winmodems and Rambus on a list of crappy hardware ideas foisted
by marketroids.

I think somebody should bell the cat, and at least check if Knoppix or
similar boots cleanly on the Acer 5002.

-Siva

Message: 2
Date: Wed, 13 Jul 2005 09:29:01 +0530
From: "Balaji G" <balajig@future.futsoft.com>
Subject: [Ilugc] Fedora Core 4 A crisp Review
To: <ilugc@ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <000001c5875f$343bbbe0$5175cb0a@future.futsoft.com>
Content-Type: text/plain; charset="iso-8859-1"

Hi People

I installed Fedora Core 4 yesterday on my machine which has 256 MB RAM and a
Celeron 1.7 Ghz Processor and i would say that its really good when compared
to Fedora Core 3 in terms of speed. Its really faster than FC3 but i faced a
problem in Fedora Core 4 with regards to Xorg. i.e. what happened was when
the X-Server is running and when i press Ctrl + Alt + F1 i just got a blank
screen and i was unable to access any of the terminals from F1-F6 and then i
tried searching it in Bugzilla and came to know that its a known bug so i
had to replace the file libvgahw.a with FC3's libvgahw.a and the problem got
solved.

People who are facing this problem could check out this
https://bugzilla.redhat.com/bugzilla/show_bug.cgi?id=161242


Other than this i would say Fedora Core 4 is a real good distro..


HTH
Regards
Balaji

> My main complaint is that Acer chose an SiS chipset with UMA instead
> of going with separate AGP graphics, for both the 3002 and 5002. I
> detest integrated shared-memory graphics - it rates only slightly better
> than Winmodems and Rambus on a list of crappy hardware ideas foisted

Almost every notebook available in India comes with integrated
graphics with shared mem with very few exceptions. Of the Acer models
TM4002WLCi and TM4601WLMi come with discrete AGP (ATI Mobility Radeon
X700 with 64MB RAM).  They cost 65K and 72K respectively including a
copy of Win XP Pro. I wrote to Acer and got a response saying TM4601
is also available with Linux OS. Am waiting for the dealer to send me
the price of this. In other brands any model with a discrete AGP is
abv 1 lakh.

Interestingly, another Acer model, Aspire 5500 series (with abv
mentioned graphics card) and almost similar config is available in
Thailand for 50K INR (linux OS)! Considering that it costs just 14K
for a return ticket to Bangkok one can get a notebook and a holiday in
Bangkok for the same price :-)

mano

Message: 5
Date: Wed, 13 Jul 2005 11:10:13 +0530
From: Bhuvaneswaran A <bhuvaneswaran@gmail.com>
Subject: Re: [Ilugc] samba file save problem
To: Bala Vignesh <kbalavignesh@gmail.com>
Cc: ilugc@ae.iitm.ac.in
Message-ID: <4dc6c90405071222404e747c5c@mail.gmail.com>
Content-Type: text/plain; charset=ISO-8859-1

>  In server the files have rwxrw-r-- permission
> on client ( mounted) files have the rw-r--r-- permission

You should permit the samba client to edit the file. You can configure
it in /etc/samba/smb.conf. You should set 'writable = yes' or
something alike. Dig into it for further details.

From: andyetitmoves at gmail.com (Ramkumar R)
Date: Wed Jul 13 12:58:15 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] RE: ilugc Digest

References: <372DD7320F873B43929D49BFF86F950B0E3B0135@mail3.hexaware.com>

>   "recursive search a string inside folders & subfolders till the end  & to replace that string"

find <folder> -type f -print0 | xargs -0 ./replacefile s/<search
pattern>/<replacement>/

replacefile:

#!/bin/sh

TEMP=`mktemp -t replacefile.XXXXXX` || exit 1
PAT="$1"
shift

for i in "$@"; do
  sed -e $PAT < "$i" > $TEMP && mv $TEMP "$i"
done

# replacefile ends here

it moves on...

From knutties at gmail.com  Wed Jul 13 14:19:19 2005
From: knutties at gmail.com (Natarajan K)
Date: Wed Jul 13 14:19:31 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] RE: ilugc Digest
In-Reply-To: <9a9bfc170507130027c310de4@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/13/05, Ramkumar R <andyetitmoves@gmail.com> wrote:
> >   "recursive search a string inside folders & subfolders till the end  & to replace that string"
> 
> find <folder> -type f -print0 | xargs -0 ./replacefile s/<search
> pattern>/<replacement>/

Perl has in built in place text replacement facility:

$ find <folder> -type f -print0 | \
xargs perl -pi -e 's/<find>/<replace>/g'

If you need a backup of the files with name .bak use
$ find <folder> -type f -print0 | \
xargs perl -pi.bak -e 's/<find>/<replace>/g'


HTH,
Natarajan
-- 
http://puggy.symonds.net/~natarajan

changes and I am in X, there seems to be a temporary freeze...I had
posted in cpufreq regarding this

thread in http://news.gmane.org/gmane.linux.kernel.cpufreq ... it's in
the first page)...and it turned out that it is probably a motherboard
problem (mine is Acer Aspire 3002NLC, may be other models are better
off)...so I guess Riyaz should keep this in mind...Anyway, I am
doubtful if cpufreq should affect the problem I have...

From sundaram at redhat.com  Wed Jul 13 17:08:36 2005
From: sundaram at redhat.com (Rahul Sundaram)
Date: Wed Jul 13 17:08:57 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] FC4 & internet connectivity
In-Reply-To: <495e4512050713022646feee63@mail.gmail.com>
References: <495e4512050713022646feee63@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <42D4FD3C.6090006@redhat.com>

ashwin kesavan iyengar wrote:

>Hi,
>       I have been using fc3 for a long time b4 i upgraded to fc4.
>Ever since i upgraded to fc4 i have been unable to connect to the
>internet. I have configured my broadband(BSNL's Dataone) connection to
>start up during bootup. During bootup i get the message "Bringing up
>ppp0 [ok]". Even in network system configuration shows ppp0 to be
>active. By i am not able to  browse with firefox or mozilla or lynx.
>During bootup there is a message that "Bringing up interface eth0
>[failed]". But this has been the message even during FC3, but then i
>was able to browse the web. Its able to connect to the internet from
>the windows on the same machine. Mine is a Pentium III 500 MHz
>machine.
>  
>
Daemons would generally log the messages in /var/log/messages. See if 
there are AVC denied messages in /var/log/audit.log as specified in 
http://fedora.redhat.com/docs/release-notes/fc4/#sn-audit-daemon. If so 
the SELinux policies might be preventing DHCP access if you using it. 
You can set disable SELinux protection for DHCP in 
system-config-securitylevel or set SELinux itself to permissive to check 
this issue

regards
Rahul
From shuveb at gmail.com  Wed Jul 13 17:45:22 2005
From: shuveb at gmail.com (Shuveb Hussain)
Date: Wed Jul 13 17:46:54 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] IP Encryption
Message-ID: <c24555040507130515160e3d05@mail.gmail.com>

Hi All,
Consider the followinf situation:

One server and several clients connecting to it. All these clients
will typically access the server for VNC. Communication on this LAN is
only between clients and the server. There is no inter-client
communication as such like on normal LANs.

What I now need to do is to encrypt IP traffic between the server and
the clients. I tried out IPSec (openswan), but that does not seem to
be the solution since its most natural use is creation of tunnels
between two gateways(with a network behind them). Here I want to
encrypt IP traffic between two hosts that are directly connected.

Are there any other suggestions on this regard?
TIA.

--shuveb

informs me that I was correct, what pppoe in GNU/Linux
said was absolutely correct. He is now eager to learn
to setup pppoe on GNU/Linux for better
troubleshooting!

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Wed Jul 13 21:01:05 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Wed Jul 13 20:44:06 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (SETFONT)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0507132041340.869-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

International Open Source Network (IOSN) is released a detailed FOSS
Localization Guide to assists people in localizing FOSS applications.
URL: http://www.iosn.net/l10n/localization-guide/ (Thanks MadhanRaj)

One Day One Command 
===================

setfont -- Load EGA/VGA console screen font.

Summary:

The setfont command reads a font file and loads it into the EGA/VGA
character generator and optionally outputs the previous font.  It can
also load various mapping tables and output the previous versions. The
standard Linux font format is the PSF (PC Screen Format) font.

Examples:

$ setfont -- Load the default font.

$ setfont -v -- Load the default font with verbose output.

$ setfont iso01.14 -- Load the iso01 font (size=8x14).

/lib/kbd/consolefonts - Default Dir for console fonts.
/lib/kbd/unimaps      - Default Dir for Unicode maps.
/lib/kbd/consoletrans - Default Dir for screen mappings.
Read the ReadMe files available in the above locations to get more 
information about the font and maps.

TIP: Set your default console font in /etc/sysconfig/i18n file.

Read: man setfont

Bye :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

--- Viveka nanda <viveka.ananda@gmail.com> wrote:

> Dear Group,
>  I am having windows 98SE on my machine, yesterday i installed
> redhat9.0 in 
> partition E, i m having three partitions c,d and e. i went to
> custom 
> installation and installed all the applications, installations was 
> successful, i created one user account also, but now when i m
> logging on to 
> user i m not able to see my windows partions and after inserting
> the CD i m 
> not able to read it too when i click cdrom it shows nothing in it,
> can 
> anyone help?

redhat 9 will not automount windows partition. You need to do it
manualy e.g. Mandrake will do this.

first create a suitable directory like /mnt/windows_c or any other
place you want.

mount /dev/hda1 /mnt/windows_c 

where /dev/hda1 is your C drive hda2 is D etc.

Look at man mount for more information.

Similaryly redhat 9 will not auto mount cds.First right click on
icon,
select mount and then try to access with double click.

Raman.P

> I guess you wanted to ask in the mailing-list?

> Anyway, if you were asking me only: ssh needs the applications to use
> proxy'd ports for ssh tunneling to take place. it is not transparent
> unless you want to have one ssh tunnel for each possible port/service
> that needs to be secured.
> 
> IPsec operates at IP level, with out requiring applications to be
> knowing that their data is being sent through an encrypted channel.

Oh ok. But I read a year or so back Bruce Schneier condemning IPSec as
being too complex to be secure.

Hi,
> yesterday.. firefox was taking all my CPU and ram, i think its because
> of opening a specific site... but the browser should have a feature
> which restricts it from going into a deadlock noo...

I find that when gmail is open, and it is trying to load something, or
it is refreshing the main inbox page, firefox takes up a steady 10 to
20% CPU. This seems to be noticeable only when the connection goes
down half way through the refresh and the refresh does not complete -
and hence the browser gets stuck permanently trying to refresh.
Perhaps its polling the socket or something during the XMLHTTP call?
Usually pressing the stop button and refreshing manually fixes the
problem... Its not too serious a problem considering that only 10 to
20% CPU is used up... atleast not much for a desktop user...

Subject: [Ilugc] Fedora Core 4
In-Reply-To: <42D3D5E7.5000502@redhat.com>
References: <000501c586df$b7e69c60$5175cb0a@future.futsoft.com>
	<a8f9901205071207082300f323@mail.gmail.com>
	<6.2.3.4.2.20050712195015.03121e10@frodo.hserus.net>
	<42D3D5E7.5000502@redhat.com>
Message-ID: <a8f99012050714194923ff832f@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/12/05, Rahul Sundaram <sundaram@redhat.com> wrote:
> Suresh Ramasubramanian wrote:
> 
> > At 07:38 PM 7/12/2005, Sivasankar Chander wrote:
> >
> >> 3) Get rid of udev, hal, etc. and downgrade to a static /dev tree.
> >
> >
> > why?  i haven't found udev to be a significant performance hog
> >
> > hald and dbus on the other hand .. well they aren't too bad but you
> > might have a point there
> 
> None of them are really resource hogs and these are fundamental
> advancements which you cannot really downgrade without breaking a whole
> lot of user space apps sitting on top of it.  In fact for FC5 the whole
> init system is potentially dependant on dbus
> 
> http://fedoraproject.org/wiki/FCNewInit
> https://www.redhat.com/archives/fedora-devel-list/2005-June/msg01390.html
> 
>
   I don't dispute that udev, etc., are the way to go for the future. 
However, there are certain applications for which I prefer a static
/dev tree. Why do this? Some possible reasons:

1) Smaller memory footprint, better stability and performance - YMMV.
2) Dependencies from an old userland that require a static /dev/tree,
    for instance, Cryptoloop implementations that expect to find certain
    /dev/loop* entries.
3) For easy filesystem recovery using non-udev recovery CDs.
4) For kernel experimentation.
 
 On FC3, it is possible to downgrade to a static /dev tree without
breaking most of userland. YMMV - as always, perform a backup
before trying this out. You may have other dependencies
which I did not encounter:

1) Rebuild (from SRPM) and install the following RPMs (Google and obtain
them from previous Fedora/RedHat releases):

kudzu-1.1.36.3-1
kudzu-devel-1.1.36.3-1
hotplug_2004_04_01-1.1
hwdata-0.103.1-1

2) Downgrade to gnome-vfs2-2.6.0-8 (again, rebuild from SRPM):

# you can rebuild these later
rpm -e eel2 eog gedit

rpm -Uvh --oldpackage gnome-vfs2-2.6.0-8.386.rpm
     gnome-vfs2-devel-2.6.0-8,i386.rpm
     gnome-vfs2-smb-2.6.0-8.i386.rpm

3) Get rid of hal and udev:

rpm -e hal

# (stop udev)
rpm -e udev --nodeps

# reboot
rpm -Uvh --oldpackage dev-3.3.12.3-1.i386.rpm MAKEDEV-3.3.8-2.i386.rpm
# ignore lots of warnings

4) Adjust /etc/fstab and verify that everything still works OK.

Voila! You have an FC3 installation with a static /dev tree now.

(The main reason that I jumped through all these hoops was to downgrade
to a patched version of util-linux-2.11y-29 from FC1, which I needed to 
support Loop-Crypto using CryptoAPI transparently. )

-Siva

Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (PRINTENV)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0507150954530.16830-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Revolution OS is a English documentary movie, about Linux based OS,
directed by Mr J.T.S.Moore. The DVD contains sub-titles for No .of
Languages. If you want to contribute for any of the Indian Language
sub-titles, Kindly contact Mr Shakthi "cyborg4k at yahoo dot com".

One Day One Command 
===================

printenv - Print All/Part of Environment

Summary:

`printenv' prints environment variables with its Name and Value.

Examples:

$ printenv -- Print all Env variables and its value.

$ printenv HOSTNAME -- Print HOSTNAME value.

$ printenv SHELL TERM -- Print SHELL and TERM values.

Read: man printenv

 An year ago I had setup an OpenLDAP server and the server was basically
used as a centralized user management and as an authentication server for
the GNU/Linux and Sun Solaris boxes. While setting up the server I had
created a CA Certificate in the server for the purpose of using TLS/SSL
for communication between the server and the client. The certificate got
expired and I had created a new one (In the server) and replaced the old
one. But when I try to authenticate using one of the client (RedHat AS
2.1), I am getting "Access Denied" message. If I log into the client as
ROOT (The ROOT account is still in the "/etc/passwd" file) and execute
the "/usr/sbin/authconfig" command and remove the TLS option, then the
authentication works. The question is "Do I have to do any changes in the
client side for the TLS to work?". When setting up the client for the
first time (i.e. an year ago), I did not do any change on the client
machine except running the "authconfig" command and entering the relevant
details. Any suggestions or pointers would be appreciated. Thank You.

Muthu

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Fri Jul 15 18:17:38 2005
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar Babu)
Date: Fri Jul 15 18:18:22 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Mandrake 10.1 - sound Problem with Kmix
In-Reply-To: <dc538c3f050715012776f6bd9a@mail.gmail.com>
References: <dc538c3f050715012776f6bd9a@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <op.styghoizv8spko@xaero.intranet.vetrije.com>

On Fri, 15 Jul 2005 13:57:14 +0530, bala chandar <mbchandar@gmail.com>  
wrote:

> Hi,
>
> I have been using mdk 10.1. if i configureKmix to have the full sound,  
> it affectsonly at that session. if i restart themachine, its not getting  
> affected. help plz!

Enable 'sound' and 'alsa' service for
your current runlevel. You could try
the following commands as root user on
the console/terminal:
  ln -s /etc/init.d/sound /etc/rc0.d/K69sound
  ln -s /etc/init.d/sound /etc/rc6.d/K69sound
  ln -s /etc/init.d/sound /etc/rc3.d/S18sound
  ln -s /etc/init.d/sound /etc/rc5.d/S18sound

  ln -s /etc/init.d/alsa /etc/rc0.d/K70alsa
  ln -s /etc/init.d/alsa /etc/rc6.d/K70alsa
  ln -s /etc/init.d/sound /etc/rc3.d/S17alsa
  ln -s /etc/init.d/sound /etc/rc5.d/S17alsa

Alternatively, there should be some gui-tool
on Mandrake that lets you automate this task
(enabling/disabling via checkbox).

Hope this solves the problem.

--
Chandrashekar Babu.
http://www.chandrashekar.info/

Date: Fri Jul 15 18:51:00 2005

On 7/15/05, aravamuthan <sriaara@yahoo.com> wrote:
> "root user not able to login, but others ok".


1. username 'root' may not exist.
2. password could have been changed.
3. securetty has incorrect/inappropriate entry.
4. one of the .dot files could have been 'hacked' by naughty users to
have logout or exit.
5. the passwd entry could have had an invalid shell


A dozen other reasons. Research a bit. Be a bit more clear. Provide us
error messages/log files.

/arvind

On 7/15/05, Anto Paul <antopaul@gmail.com> wrote:
> 
> Mobilis.
> http://www.hindu.com/2005/05/11/stories/2005051103002200.htm
> 

FWIW, one of the companies that builds Simputers (Vinay Deshpande's
Encore Computers) is also behind the Mobilis design, and I wouldn't
be surprised if it shared a common platform with the Simputer - AFAIK,
Mobilis is not x86-based, and does not have a hard disk. It's more like
a mobile thin-client or POS-terminal, aimed at industry verticals like
logistics, freight/package handling, etc. It's not a general-purpose, 
PC-architecture laptop.

If you want a general-purpose x86 laptop, there isn't a better deal than
the Acer Travelmate 2355 for Rs.27500 today - it's a very nice almost
fully-loaded 1.4 GHz Dothan Celeron M. If it's in a socket, there's no
reason it can't be upgraded to a Pentium M at 2 GHz or higher (the
Celeron M and the Pentium M are pin-compatible).

-Siva

On 7/15/05, vsriramk@sify.com <vsriramk@sify.com> wrote:
>i also tried out another option
> # etc/hostname and #etc/hosts but it didn't work.
> please let me know the other files where i need to change the name.

Yes, that is sufficient if you want the changes made temporarily. Just
make sure the services are restarted to see the effects of changes.
Simplest way is to just press Control-D (logout).

To make the changes permanent look for distribution specific
configuration files where 'HOSTNAME' or 'hostname' variables are
defined.

-- 
Arvind Kalyan

Greetings!

I would like to thank the Tiruchirapalli MYSQL group
and CSE department faculty, students, and the
management of Saranathan College of Engineering,
Tiruchirapalli for giving me an opportunity to conduct
a one-day GNU/Linux workshop.

Thanks to Ramkumar L, S. Srinivasan, T. Shivakumar,
Arul Jeeva, and Lakshminarayanan of Tiruchirapalli
MYSQL group, http://www.harshainfotech.com/, and
http://www.rajaramsystems.com/. 

http://mysql.meetup.com/70/

Special thanks to Ramkumar L who has been working with
me in planning this event for the past two weeks.
Thanks to Prof. Venkatasubramanian, HOD, CSE
Department, Saranathan College of Engineering for
coordinating the sessions.

http://www.saranathan.ac.in/

The workshop was announced in the newspapers, The
Indian Express and The Hindu. The photos of the
workshop (and the trip) can be viewed from here:

http://www.shakthimaan.com/Mambo/gallery/album12

The MYSQL group is working on using LAMP on GNU/Linux
for the Pulivazham village cooperative society milk
center farmers. They require to keep track of
accounts, volume of milk stored in the facilities, and
general book-keeping activities. 

Ramkumar L: Regarding the contacts:

1. Sarvannan (Lucas-TVS) - told me during Raman's talk
on LTSP that they supply Linux drivers for their
printers. So, Pulivazham center printers should work
with GNU/Linux.

2. Gaurav - from http://www.gnulinuxclub.org is
interested in php, web admin. He should start building
a database of companies working/using LAMP in India
for career opportunities. You can let him know of
harshainfotech.com and your services.

3. Sivasankar Chander - told me at MIT, "Carte
Blanche" 2005 about 'Cascade Systems & Solutions',
Plaza center near Gemini circle, about HP E-Vectra
systems that are about Rs.5000/-. He runs FC on it.
So, for low-cost solutions, you might want to check
this out.

4. Bharathi S - and other networking gurus, might
provide some contacts/tips on line-of-sight solutions
for networking all the villages together. Folks, right
now they have a dial-up offer from BSNL at Rs.25/- per
hour :o.

Good luck to the Tiruchirapalli MYSQL team for this
project. Hopefully next time when we visit you guyz,
we will see Pulivazham farmers using GNU/Linux for
their day-to-day activities.

Thanking you all once again,

SK

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Sun Jul 17 04:56:55 2005
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Sun Jul 17 17:27:27 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] dishnet configuration in suse 9.2 pro
In-Reply-To: <20050717104632.6463.qmail@web32109.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20050717115655.70833.qmail@web50203.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi,

--- konjeti sreeram <sreeramat2000@yahoo.com> wrote:
>   i am sreeram.recently i established dishnet
> internet
> connection in my computer.

How? What is your network setup?

> I/P :192.168.26.5

How is that dishnet is giving you a private IP
address?

> subnet Mask: 230.230.230.0
> default gateway : 192.168.90.5
> DNS server :192.168.90.5
>             202.90.230.9
>             202.90.250.7
> 
> how can i configure these ip address in suse 9.2
> linux. 

GUI: Use YaST
Command line: Use "ifconfig" (as root)

# ifconfig eth0 192.168.26.5 netmask 230.230.230.0
gateway 192.168.90.5 

In your /etc/resolv.conf you can add your DNS servers
like this:

nameserver    202.90.230.9
nameserver    202.90.250.7

> if any additional packages required plese send me
> and
> give website address.

Post the output of:

/sbin/lsmod
/sbin/ifconfig -a
/sbin/route -n

Regards,

SK

Deepan Chakravarthy N wrote:
> Hello,
>    I am planning to take linux  certification exam. I am not much
> aware of which certification to take and which place to go for
> coaching. I would like the experts here to guide me to choose a good
> place. I am prepared to study on my own but would still look for a
> institution which would teach me the difficult things alone. I cant
> afford a big sum of money for this .. so please tell me a economical
> one. I would prefer to stay with redhat certification.

I am planning to take RHCE at STG within a week..
I heard it was the best in chennai.

Rs 13200 for the course
we have an option of 3 months(2hr per day) or 2 months(3hr per day).

Rs 10000 for the exam. so total is around 23000..

they promise 96hrs of classes(all practical)
i do not know how they will make it to go to 3 months..

u do not have to write the exam immedietly after the course..
u can take ur own time..
but if u fail, Rs 10,000 is gone with the wind..

u should pay another 10,000 to write the exam again..

certification is current for 2 releases of RHEL
that is around 3 years from Feb 2005 if u write in RHEL 4.

if u are new to linux/unix, 96 hrs will help you cover only the basics. 
IMHO i do not think a newbie will be ready for RHCE just after
96 hrs of teaching..u can just get ur feet wet in 96 hrs.

if u are confortable with basics then go ahead..
if not, take a couple of months to learn RH linux.
once u learn the basics u will atleast be able to grasp what the tutor
means to say.


As far as teaching goes I guess it all depends on the person teaching
you.. if he is well versed, u should be ready to extract information
from him. not every one who knows unix is as nice as the people in this
forum. i know some unix/solaris/linux admins who never open their mouth
to share their knowledge.. they guard it as if it is their family secret.

a lot of people think LINUX = REDHAT. and lot of them happen to be
in the HR dept of some big companies.. So RHCE will work better than 
other linux certfications in India as far as employment is concerned.

If u plan to write the exam without training..
check out these links.

https://www.redhat.com/apps/training/assess/faq.html
https://www.redhat.com/apps/training/assess/

redhat says

-------------
Red Hat's Pre-assessment tests help prospective course participants 
determine whether they possess the knowledge taught in particular Red 
Hat courses so they can choose the appropriate class for their level of 
skill and knowledge.
---------------

so ... good luck...

if u r interested in STG i can give u the no of the person to contact
for more details...

if any one knows abt the pass/fail percentage in RHCE exam pls let me know.

Regards
Easwaran.K.V

the redhat preassessment is good.
It tests u in almost all areas of linux administration.
then it gives a report of what all u are strong in and in wat u aren't.(and

true.

On 17/07/05, Arvind Kalyan <base16@gmail.com> wrote:
> On 7/17/05, Easwaran.K.V <kveaswaran@gmail.com> wrote:
> > Rs 13200 or Rs 10000
> 
> Personally, I think both. And together it becomes a bit too much for a 'course.'
> 
> To prove that you know Linux you could a lot more than show a
> certificate. Among other things 1) Projects, 2) Publications, 3) Work
> experience, etc.

I think the numbers are par for the course. Have you checked the
prices of comparable certification from others recently? Like Cisco or
Juniper or Oracle or Sun? (Microsoft doesn't count :)

The RHCE is priced at $749 (exam alone) internationally; I find the
Indian prices cheap compared to that. And given the gruelling day long
hands-on exam, it is well worth the price.

I have been hiring Linux admins recently, and I find people tend to
lie about or over-enhance their roles in the three enumerated points
above. I am inclined to trust the certification under such
circumstances. I am sure others hiring in the field think like me.

Binand

PS: Resume says: "Instrumental in migrating a large CRM database from
Windows 2000 Server/MS-SQL to RHEL3/Oracle". Truth: Tier-1 support
AFTER the migration. Or: "Senior Administrator for a large website
serving many 100k customers every day". Truth: Job is to run "service
httpd restart" every now and then. And so on...

For Oracle, 

Min RAM = 512 MB 
/tmp = 2 GB 
ORACLE_HOME= /oracle/product/10g 
ORACLE_HOME = 5 GB
/temp = 1 GB 

some kernel modfications. 

There are two patchs to be installed from oracle site.

Rameshkumar

Message-ID: <1121631401.3815.105.camel@localhost.localdomain>

-------- Forwarded Message --------
From: Matt Oquist <moquist@softwarefreedomday.org>
To: moquist@softwarefreedomday.org
Subject: SFD 2005: Request your sponsored SFD CDs and materials!
Date: Mon, 11 Jul 2005 01:01:27 -0400
Dear SFD Team Leaders,

In 2004, SFD was successful because many of your volunteer teams around
the world burned CDs and distributed them in celebration of Free and
Open Source Software.  2005 holds new promise for Software Freedom Day
because a primary sponsor (Canonical, Ltd.) has promised to donate up
to 100 professionally pressed and packaged SFD CDs[1] to each of the
first 150 SFD teams to register and request materials!

We don't yet have the final figures, but we will also be providing
a limited number of free SFD T-shirts, SFD balloons (you'll need your
own helium) and SFD temporary tattoos for the first teams to request
materials.

There are a few criteria for teams to qualify for sponsored supplies:

* Your team must be registered on our registration form (teams from
last year, please register again).

* Your team must have set up a wiki page with at least the basic
information about members and plans. The more detail, the better.
Please provide a URL.

* You must have made an initial forum post inviting others to join your
team.  (Go to http://softwarefreedomday.org, click "Forum" at the top
of the page.)

* Your team must have at least 3 members.  (More is better.)

* You must completely fill out the request form with a valid postal
address where we can ship your materials.

These and other details are discussed on the SFD Materials Request
Form, which is on our website.  (Go to http://softwarefreedomday.org,
click on "Get Materials" in the menu on the left side.)

Approximately 191 registered team leaders are receiving this email, so
you should meet the criteria and apply for sponsorship within the next
few days to ensure that your team receives the sponsored supplies.

We're very excited about the potential we have to impact the world
with Software Freedom Day 2005, and we hope you can take advantage of
our sponsor's generous offer in order to make your celebrations even
more successful.

Regards,
Matt Oquist, Software Freedom International

TODO: Request supplies at
http://softwarefreedomday.org/index.php?option=com_mosforms&mosform=2&Itemid=62

[1] This year's SFD CDs will be TheOpenCD 3.0, which is a single-disc
combination of an x86 Ubuntu LiveCD and TheOpenCD with updated
packages.

> Message: 6
> Date: Sun, 17 Jul 2005 04:56:55 -0700 (PDT)
> From: Shakthi Kannan <cyborg4k@yahoo.com>
> Subject: Re: [Ilugc] dishnet configuration in suse 9.2 pro
> To: ilugc@ae.iitm.ac.in
> Message-ID: <20050717115655.70833.qmail@web50203.mail.yahoo.com>
> Content-Type: text/plain; charset=iso-8859-1
> 
> Hi,
> 
> --- konjeti sreeram <sreeramat2000@yahoo.com> wrote:
> >   i am sreeram.recently i established dishnet
> > internet
> > connection in my computer.
> 
> How? What is your network setup?
> 
> > I/P :192.168.26.5
> 
> How is that dishnet is giving you a private IP
> address?
> 
> > subnet Mask: 230.230.230.0
> > default gateway : 192.168.90.5
> > DNS server :192.168.90.5
> >             202.90.230.9
> >             202.90.250.7
> >
> > how can i configure these ip address in suse 9.2
> > linux.
> 
> GUI: Use YaST
> Command line: Use "ifconfig" (as root)
> 
> # ifconfig eth0 192.168.26.5 netmask 230.230.230.0
> gateway 192.168.90.5
> 
> In your /etc/resolv.conf you can add your DNS servers
> like this:
> 
> nameserver    202.90.230.9
> nameserver    202.90.250.7
> 
> > if any additional packages required plese send me
> > and
> > give website address.
> 
> Post the output of:
> 
> /sbin/lsmod
> /sbin/ifconfig -a
> /sbin/route -n
> 
> Regards,
> 
> SK

Hi,

   As far as RHCE is concerned its the leading certification in linux
though you have other line LPI and Novell's.

  I think there is two options available in STG. There own certificate
and course material for the course and Second is official Redhat. If
you are so much sure of taking RHCE then with RHCE certificate no one
bothers about what course certificate you have.

   If you are planning to take up RHCE after the course in STG but
after 2-3 months you make sure that you inform the manager you will
take a break and take the Night Labs before the exam which you are
entitled to.

  Also as far as the percentage of pass there is no restriction like
only this many no. can pass and others should be failed. If you need
the percentage (marks) then see the redhat website for latest
information.

  I would also like to tell those who take up RHCE to be good with all
the excercise in the Redhat Study material as with that you will able
to around 70% of marks. This i am telling through the experience and i
got my certification in june 2004.

  Also getting 100% in RHCE is not something too hard (Believe me as i
was able to get it) if you practice well and if you are clear about
concepts and read the questions in RHCE exam properly as they wont be
straight-forward but again wont be too much twisted.

  If you are a group who is practicing for RHCE then first prepare a
method which you are going to follow to get the best result. Team work
is always good. ( we were 6 in a group when we took the exam and we
all got certified in first attempt.).

 The most important thing in our case was we made the best use of the
infrastructure available in STG. Which again you can do.

 If you have any other clarification you can mail me or call me at 98407-46415.

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Mon Jul 18 19:35:22 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Mon Jul 18 19:16:31 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (CHKCONFIG)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0507181912000.4526-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

IndiX (Indian Language support for GNU/Linux OS), A modified X server
to support Indian languages using OpenType Fonts. Uses Unicode. 
URL: http://rohini.ncst.ernet.in/indix (Thanks FUG-Bglr)

One Day One Command 
===================

chkconfig -- Update/Show runlevel information for system services.

Summary:

'chkconfig' provides a simple command-line tool for maintaining the
/etc/rc[0-6].d directory hierarchy by relieving system administrators
of the task of directly manipulating the numerous symbolic links in
those directories.

A runlevel is a software configuration of the system which allows only
a selected group of processes to exist (man init).

Examples:

$ chkconfig --list -- List runlevel info for all system services.

$ chkconfig --list xinetd -- List runlevel info of xinetd service.

# chkconfig --add newser -- Add a new service for management.

# chkconfig --del oldser -- Remove this services symbolic links from 
                            all rc[0-6].d Dirs.

# chkconfig --level 35 xinetd on -- Start the xinetd service only in 
                                    runlevel 3 and 5.

Read: man chkconfig

Bye :)

Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

Hi,

Red Hat has an opening for a Technical Translator for Tamil to be
based out of Pune.

The profile includes translation, development and editing of content
for software localisation, paper, multimedia or web-based
publications. Further on it also includes translation of message
catalogs into the native language for Red Hat and other selected Open
Source software. Participation in Quality Assurance activities
focussed on i18n and l10n are also an important job function. It also
includes carrying forward the existing corpus of work and adding to it
through best practices and community interaction.

Exposure to the local language, language standards, computing inputs
and prior experience of l10n would be an advantage.

Those interested may send in the CV in OpenOffice.org/HTML/ASCII text
format to sankar@redhat.com with [Technical Translator - Tamil] in the
subject line.

Dont use telnet, use ssh

And find out what shell you are using as root - freebsd uses /bin/sh, 
not bash, for root, by default

wrote:

> Is there any way to run the root account's.profile, without restarting  
> the computer?

Try the following command:
  . /root/.profile

[Note the . followed by a space and then
  the path to the root's .profile].

in your .profile, try:

FOO=bar; export FOO

JAVA_HOME=/usr/local/diablo-jdk1.3.1

TERM=${TERM:-cons25}

PAGER=more

On Tue, 19 Jul 2005 17:12:13 +0530, Joseph Kulandai <kulandai@gmail.com>  
wrote:

>
> This command says,
> /bin/csh

Well well, you'll need to add your environment
variables into /root/.cshrc file rather. The
.profile will not be executed by tcsh shell.

The syntax of (t)csh scripts are a lot
different from (ba|k)sh scripts. Anyways,
here's something that you might want to
try out. Edit /root/.cshrc file and add
the following line:
  set JAVA_HOME /usr/local/diablo-jdk1.3.1

'man csh' to learn more about csh.

If you aren't comfortable with csh, you
can change your default shell to /bin/sh
  (or your favourite shell) by running
the chsh command.

--
Chandrashekar Babu.
http://www.chandrashekar.info/

On Tue, 19 Jul 2005 19:56:02 +0530,
Rajagopal Natarajan <rajagopal.n@gmail.com> wrote:

> I couldn't find the system requirementsfor user-mode-linux in that  
> website.
> Can you plz let me know that?

It depends on what you wish to do with it. I remember
using user-mode-linux on a Pentium III 550 MHz with
128 MB RAM running 5 user-mode-linux sessions and
an X Server + lean desktop running on the host.
The 5 uml sessions were setup with a virtual
network connection and one of them were running
apache web server accessible via other sessions
simultaneously via text-mode web browsers. Each
session would add an overhead of about 16 MB memory
(excluding any startup services/programs that you
might want to keep running in that session).

What you need in excess in disk-space to create
image file for each session. This image file
would be mounted via loopback and accessed as the
rootfs by a uml session. But with 40-80 GB hard
disks in vogue today, this shouldn't pose a
constraint.

To summarise, you can setup UML on a desktop class
machine for testing/learning purpose without much
issues.

--
Chandrashekar Babu.
http://www.chandrashekar.info/
From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Tue Jul 19 20:32:12 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Tue Jul 19 20:14:40 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (FSCK)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0507192006200.804-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Gipi, a console based jumble like puzzle game is developed by 
Mr Dinker Charak. URL: http://sarovar.org/projects/gipi/

One Day One Command 
===================

fsck -- Linux File System Check and Repair Tool.

Summary:

'fsck' is used to check and optionally repair one or more Linux file
systems. If no file-systems are specified on the command line, fsck
will default to checking file-systems in /etc/fstab file.

In actuality, fsck is simply a front-end for the various file system
checkers (fsck.cramfs, fsck.ext2, fsck.ext3, fsck.jfs, fsck.msdos,
fsck.reiserfs, fsck.vfat, ...) available under GNU/Linux OS.

Examples:

# fsck -- Check all file systems available in /etc/fstab.

$ fsck -N -- Don't execute. Just show what would be done.

# fsck -V -- Show detailed output, including all file system-specific
             commands that are executed.

# fsck -a -- Automatically repair the file system without asking for
             confirmations. (By default, ask for conformation).

# fsck /dev/hda2 -- Check the HDA2 device/partition.

# fsck /usr/local -- Check the /usr/local mount point.

# fsck LABEL=usr -- Check file-system, which has a label matching 
                    to "usr".

Read: man fsck

Bye :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

See a lot of posts in this list openly abusing copyrighted material.
Pls remember that the GPL itself is held in place by the copyright
laws. If we are to preach linux (and the GPL) with any sense of moral
authority, for heavens sake, start respecting copyright laws (and
other laws too).

Spend that few hundred ruppees to 'buy' books. Reading from a book is
a lot less strain on the eyes than reading soft copies and you can
read it anywhere - dinner table, bathroom, bus, train etc. And it is
less messy than handling photostat copies. In fact I wouldnt be
surprised if the cost of photostat is almost the same as the cost of
the book - and it will last longer!

From Noorul.Islam at caritor.com  Wed Jul 20 13:47:53 2005
From: Noorul.Islam at caritor.com (Noorul Islam)
Date: Wed Jul 20 13:50:47 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] 1400x1050 resolution support in Fedora Core 4
Message-ID: <OFBC3FB002.365D3FF4-ON65257044.002D901C-65257044.002EA56D@notes.caritor.com>

Hi,

Yesterday I installed Fedora Code 4 on my Laptop (IBM ThinkPad R52 
(1860AQ1)) which has inbuilt Intel 915GM Graphics Accelarator with 128MB 
shared video memory.

In the begining X was not working properly. It showed only corrupted 
display. My LCD monitor supports 1400x1050 maximum resolution in Windows 
OS. The driver used by Linux is generic VESA. 

Actually I googled a lot regarding 915G chipset before starting the 
installation. But I couldn't find much help. In reading about this I also 
found this: http://www.geocities.com/stomljen/ which contains 
915resolution (from 855resolution) which is supposed to add a VESA mode 
for 1400x1050. I haven't attempted to use that, but some people have 
reported success. Rather you can say that I am afraid to run that program. 
You can see that the program modifies the some information @VBIOS.

I thought of changing X configuration. So I backed up my 
/etc/X11/xorg.conf and modified it. After lots of trial and error the 
following configuration helped me to bring X up.

1) commenting the following entries in "Monitor" section. 

        HorizSync   15.0 - 35.0
        VertRefresh 50.0 - 75.0

   I did this becuase the log says that refresh rate is not matching for 
the mode 1280x1020 while probing this mode. It was not even trying to 
probe 1400x1050.

2) In "Screen" section
 
   I changed the existing lines to look like this.

        DefaultDepth     24
        Subsection "Display"
                Depth    24
                Modes    "1400x1050"
                ViewPort 0 0
        EndSubsection

Now when I started X it worked. Well I am confused how it worked, because 
I commented out the HorizSync and VertRefresh entries, I think which are 
very much important. I wonder how it used 1400x1050 resolution which is 
not even probed by X while trying to choose the apt mode. 

In GNOME, it says that the resolution is 1400x1050 and the refresh rate as 
0Hz. Is this something dangeros? Well the X works fine. Windows says that 
refresh rate is 60Hz. Does anyone come across something like this? This 
0Hz is really bothering me to continue using X.


Cheers,
Noorul

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Wed Jul 20 20:34:22 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Wed Jul 20 20:16:38 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (UMOUNT)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0507202004220.15260-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

BZip2 Translator Tool is developed by Venkataraman, Ankur and Shikka.
This translator, when mapped on a file, you can do bzip compressed I/O
(Like Read, Seek, Length). 
URL: http://www.gnu-india.org/pipermail/gnu-india/20010307/000113.html

One Day One Command 
===================

umount -- UnMount File System

Summary:

The umount command detaches the file system(s) mentioned from the file
hierarchy. A file system cannot be unmounted when it is `busy', For
example, when there are open files on it, or when some process has its
working directory there, or when a swap file on it is in use.

Examples:

# umount /mnt/cdrom -- Unmount the CDROM, using mount point.

# umount -v /dev/cdrom -- Unmount the CDROM, using device file and 
                          show verbose messages.

# umount -f /nfs/home -- Force unmount (Useful in case of an
                         unreachable NFS system).

# umount -l /media/floppy -- Lazy unmount (I don't care, why the
                             device is busy).

# umount -n /mnt/cdrom -- Unmount, with-out updating the /etc/mtab,
                  which contains the list of currently mounted FSs.

Read: man umount

Bye :)

Bharathi S

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Thu Jul 21 09:32:35 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Thu Jul 21 09:14:51 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Fwd: LJ Tech Tip
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0507210927520.17953-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Tech Tip from Linux Journal:

If you're editing a Web page and want to match a color on another site
or in another application, use Muhammad A. Muquit's "grabc" program.
When you run it from the shell, your X pointer turns into a crosshairs
symbol. Move the crosshairs over the color you want and click, and
grabc gives you the color in hex and decimal.

URL: http://muquit.com/muquit/software/grabc/grabc.html

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S

From base16 at gmail.com  Thu Jul 21 17:26:58 2005
From: base16 at gmail.com (Arvind Kalyan)
Date: Thu Jul 21 17:27:12 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Setting up GPRS in Linux
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0507211657130.21029-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0507211657130.21029-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>
Message-ID: <90c25f270507210456407b4e78@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/21/05, Bharathi Subramanian <sbharathi@midascomm.com> wrote:
> Could u help me in finding the drivers for DCU-11 serial cable and
> modem script drivers for sony ericsson K500i mobile.. so that i can
> configure it and use linux..

1. Make sure you have kernel version 2.6.9 or above.
2. Compile pl2303 (as built-in or as module), and modprobe it
3. modprobe'ing pl2303 with the cable in place should show your phone
as a USB dev accessible at /dev/tts/USB0 (could be different if you
have a not-so-common setup, you can see which one through dmesg
ofcourse, or /var/log/messages depending on your logging preferences.)
4. You can use wvdial or something similar.

Use these in your init commands after ATZ:

'AT+CGDCONT=1,"IP","airtelgprs",,0,0'
'AT+CGQREQ=1,0,0,0,0,0'
'AT+CGQMIN=1,0,0,0,0,0'

To dial: '
ATD*99***1#'


Ofcourse, the 1 above in the previous line and the CGDCONT 1 should
match, they are the configuration setting index in your phone. If you
have just one setting, the above should suffice. If you have debugged
earlier you are bould to have more than one settings, in that case
either delete all of them and use 1 or specify which (1, 2, 3 4, or..
whatever) configuration is to be used.

I used k700i for airtel gprs about an year back, and i used IrDA. If
you can not proceed, reply with your questions with a clear list of
the steps you had taken to try and get it to work so I can help you
out.

Thanks and regards,

-- 
Arvind Kalyan
http://www.devforge.net/~arv

On 21 Jul 2005 16:31:04 +0530, Raja Mallik <raja.mallik@moschip.com> wrote:
> 
> 
> I have upgrade my kernel-2.4.20-8 (redhat 9) to kernel-2.6.12.
> 
> Now, my "rpm command is not working "
> 
> for eg: I get these errors as Itry any thing
> 
> rpmdb: unable to join the environment
> ...
> error: cannot open Packages database in /var/lib/rpm
> 
   This is a known issue - the workaround is:

export LD_ASSUME_KERNEL=2.2.5

<or>

export LD_ASSUME_KERNEL=2.4.1

Then rebuild the rpmdb:

rpm --rebuilddb

The longer term fix is to upgrade to rpm-4.3, but you
may have to jump through a lot of dependency hoops, including
glibc-2.3.3, to do that.

-Siva

On 7/21/05, Prashanth Mohan <prashmohan@gmail.com> wrote:
> What is locking? i dont see any such option in the applications

Locking is a mechanism to mandate exclusive access to the sound
device. Possibly your applications are accessing the audio device
directly, that simply can not happen.

Sound servers are present nowadays that overcome this problem by
acting as a mux/demux for all audio applications and the single audio
device.

Please tell the error message you get and from which specific
application if any, if applicable.

Also, http://alsa.opensrc.org/ should help.

-- 
Arvind Kalyan
http://www.devforge.net/~arv

On 7/22/05, konjeti sreeram <sreeramat2000@yahoo.com> wrote:
> hai,
>   i am sreeram.i am un able to mount cdwriter in
> ElxBiz4.0.i hava one dvd rom,and cdwriter.cdrom is
> mounting well.but problem with cdwriter.Dvd rom is in
> /dev/hdc,cdwriter in /dev/scd0.i create symbolic link
> to cdrom1 using ln -s /dev/scd0 /mnt/cdrom1.

Why? What are you trying to do actually?

> but still it's showing lockfloder.

What is that?

> in command prompt if i use
> mount command it's showing permissions denied.i
> updateed /etc/mtab ,/etc/fstab also.

You should never update mtab, it is done by the kernel. Only play with fstab.

For permission denied, are you trying to write the CD as root or normal user?

> can i chang cdwriter /dev/scd0 to /dev/hdd.

hdd will have the major,minor pointing to a ide driver. scd* has
major,minor to a scsi driver.

Depending on your [u]dev[fs] settings, your requirements can not be
met with out some fiddling.

> cdrecord --scanbus it's showing cdwriter samsung.


Good, use k3b or something similar, and please have a look at
CD-Writing howto on the web if you are looking for more precise
information.

Thanks and regards,
-- 
Arvind Kalyan

From base16 at gmail.com  Fri Jul 22 23:53:46 2005
From: base16 at gmail.com (Arvind Kalyan)
Date: Fri Jul 22 23:53:55 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT]Tata indicom Broadband doubt
In-Reply-To: <87f4f6420507221100bdaf63@mail.gmail.com>
References: <1121650363.18145.238650144@webmail.messagingengine.com>
	<87f4f6420507221100bdaf63@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <90c25f2705072211235d1108d1@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/22/05, Archana.S.R <archu.oct@gmail.com> wrote:
> PPP adapter RConnect LG LSP -340E com:
> 
>         Connection-specific DNS Suffix  . :
>         IP Address. . . . . . . . . . . . : 220.226.20.112
>         Subnet Mask . . . . . . . . . . . : 255.255.255.255
>         Default Gateway . . . . . . . . . : 220.226.20.112
> 
> i too dont know wats happeneing..!


not so uncommon. I have seen even more silly settings on an LG 3100
phone. I used to get an IP address of 255.255.255.255. Yeah, IP
address. And that also was my gateway IP.

It happens when you have hardware that depends more on software for
any use. Usually the higher end models have more capable devices.
Nokia/SE models never have these problems. And usually the case is,
these devices fail under Linux - I had no way of getting my LG 3100
transfer data under Linux. I even hacked ppp code in kernel mode to
force accepting the settings and send the packets nevertheless on that
serial port. It didn't succeed in sending the packets even though my
hack on establishing the link succeeded.

It turns out that they depend heavily on the host operating system and
its 'device driver' which is the (software) modem.

Not sure about this ADSL and Rconnect thing. Could be of a similar
type. Are you able to get it work under Linux? I think reliance
provides drivers for Linux, no?

Arvind Kalyan
http://www.devforge.net/~arv

You will need to upgrade to KDE 3.2
for Tamil to work in KDE apps.
(the default KDE for RH 9 is <3.2)
You will also need xft enabled Mozilla binaries
for Tamil to display in Mozilla.

For details, check out 
http://www.zhakanini.org/English/democd.php

From srikanth.ns at gmail.com  Sat Jul 23 17:51:50 2005
From: srikanth.ns at gmail.com (NS Srikanth)
Date: Sat Jul 23 17:56:15 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Interoperability- Any Linux equivalent of AUTOCAD?
Message-ID: <000c01c58faf$5c98e560$0201a8c0@DATAONE>

Hi all,

I posted this query some time back.

A major stumbling block to conversion to Linux at Office is the lack of
AUTOCAD equivalent in Linux.

Usually when we prepare technical reports, we keep open word processor,
presentation software and AUTOCAD also. Our colleagues send us Autocad
Drawings in .dwg format. We flit seamlessly between the three apps to make a
report, a presentation and for distribution, we open it in Openoffice and
make pdf also.

We are forced to do all this in Windows. There are youngsters who are
willing to experiment, but the above is the stumbling block.

Is there any app which can read .dwg format drawings and work with it? We
cannot force others to send us drawings in other formats. But if we are able
to do it ourselves with any other app, it will help.

Any pointers please?

NS Srikanth

Subject: [Ilugc] [Photos] GNU/Linux Workshop, July 23, 2005,
	Alagappa University, Karaikudi
Message-ID: <20050725021515.18443.qmail@web50210.mail.yahoo.com>

Greetings!

I would like to thank the Correspondent, Dr. (Tmt.)
Umayal Ramanathan, the Registrar, Mr. Dhandapani, CSE
HOD, Dr. S. Sakthivel, Alagappa University, Karaikudi
for providing me with an opportunity to conduct a
GNU/Linux workshop for the MCA students on Saturday,
July 23, 2005.

The photos taken during the presentation (and the
trip) can be viewed from:

http://www.shakthimaan.com/Mambo/gallery/album13

The labs already had Red Hat, but, it was used at a
basic programming (bash scripting, desktop usage)
level. The sessions included the career opportunities
with GNU/Linux, and on the free software available for
engineers. 

Unfortunately, the download speeds are are not that
high. I gave them Knoppix 3.6, Fedora Core 3,
The.Code.Linux.avi, C-DAC tamil fonts, and the
presentation slides in CDs. BSNL are the ones who
provide some Internet connection facilities. Sify has
netcafe centers in the city, which have much better
download speeds. Most of them have a computer at home.
I've told them to send e-mails if they require any
CDs, and we can simply send the CDs to them through
courier. 

The students were very much interested in GNU/Linux. 
You should have seen their eyes, the eagerness and
willingness to really learn, to understand the
fundamental concepts of computer science, to really
put theory into practice, as opposed to ...

I definitely said I will come again, and do a much
longer workshop for the students.

Regards,

SK

--- Arvind Kalyan <base16@gmail.com> wrote:
> You remind me of an old advertisement that used to
> come on TV, for Onida :)

> Something like :  "Owners pride, neighbors envy!"

Actually, we should aim at getting laptops running
GNU/Linux for _everyone_.

In US universities, each and every student owns a
laptop, which they bring to class, take notes with it,
do their homework with it. They work on it in the
outdoors, in the labs, in the classrooms, just
anywhere on/off-campus. Of course, you have a laptop
which you used during your under-graduate study in
college. But, how many people can afford this? Like
how mobile phones are owned by every individual,
laptops should be owned by every one in India. When
will this happen?

There are now portable systems in India, like mobilis,
 that cost about Rs.10,000/-? But again how many
people can afford that in rural places? If we have to
take technology to every nook and corner of the world,
hardware prices should come down. Brazil, a happening
place for GNU/Linux, has a tie-up with Massachusetts
Institute of Technology (MIT), Cambridge on bringing a
 USD100 (INR 5,000) laptop, of course, running
GNU/Linux. 

http://www.cnn.com/2005/WORLD/americas/06/30/brazil.laptop.ap/index.html

There are so many schools and colleges who still do
paper-work. It is extrememly simply to setup a network
running GNU/Linux machines and do all their
administration, communication etc. at an economical
price. People are just ignorant.

SK

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Tue Jul 26 21:09:17 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Tue Jul 26 21:08:33 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (APT-GET)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0507262039570.12029-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

A Team from WBUT, Kolkata, is started the efforts for Localizing the
Free/Open Source Softwares to Urdu-Indic Language.
URL: http://sourceforge.net/mailarchive/message.php?msg_id=12378942

One Day One Command 
===================

apt-get -- Debian Package Manager.

Summary:

apt-get is a powerful package manager used in the Debian Distro. It is
in-build capability to resolve the conflicts and dependencies.

Examples:

# apt-get update -- Update the Pkg listings from package repositories.

# apt-get install newpkg -- Install the 'newpkg' from repositories 
                            with all dependencies.

# apt-get upgrade -- Install newest versions of all packages currently 
                     installed.

# apt-get dist-upgrade -- Same as above. But with advanced conflict 
                          resolution capability.

# apt-get remove pkgName -- Remove the package with all needed 
                            packages.

Read: man apt-get

Debian Mirror in TamilNadu: http://ftp.iitm.ac.in/linux/
Debian Documentation  Link: http://www.debian.org/doc/
Debian CD Image Link : http://people.debian.org/cdimage/testing/

Bye :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

From knutties at gmail.com  Wed Jul 27 12:34:34 2005
From: knutties at gmail.com (Natarajan K)
Date: Wed Jul 27 12:34:46 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] rpm -U/-F
In-Reply-To: <20050727055106.89127.qmail@web31008.mail.mud.yahoo.com>

On 7/27/05, babu jayapaul <babu_jayapaul@yahoo.com> wrote:
> rpm -Uvh will remove older version and install the
> newer one.
Even if the older version does not exist, -U installs the package for you.
 
> rpm -Fvh ?.
The existence of the old version of the package is mandatory for the -F option.

"man rpm" has the necessary details :-)

Natarajan

http://puggy.symonds.net/~natarajan
From apsivam at gmail.com  Wed Jul 27 12:40:51 2005
From: apsivam at gmail.com (Sivanandhan, P.)
Date: Wed Jul 27 12:41:01 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] rpm -U/-F
In-Reply-To: <20050727055106.89127.qmail@web31008.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
References: <20050727055106.89127.qmail@web31008.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <3b020fee05072700107117318a@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/27/05, babu jayapaul <babu_jayapaul@yahoo.com> wrote:
> Hi,
> 
> what's the difference between "rpm -Uvh" and "rpm
> -Fvh".
> 
> rpm -Uvh will remove older version and install the
> newer one.
> 
> rpm -Fvh ?.
> 
> Please clarify me.
> 
> Babu. J
> 
> 

rpm -Uvh will upgrade the package if older one exist or will install
the new one.
rpm -Fvh will upgrade the package only if older one exist and will not
install if older one not found.

let see this with example.

you have a 100+ rpm files in a directory which consist of GNOME & KDE
upgrades. You are a GNOME user you want to upgrade only the newer
GNOME packages. if you did rpm -Uvh *.rpm it will upgrade GNOME
packages as well as install the new KDE packages. Where if you did rpm
-Fvh *.rpm it only upgrade already installed packages.

-- 
Cheers,
Sivam
[Jai Hind]
www.emmeskay.com

Subject: [Ilugc] viewing specific lines of file
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.58.0507270207220.655@chi.spunge.org>

Hi,
I would like to view specific lines
(range given in command line) of a file.

Say for example, I want to view line numbers
27 to 39 of file file.txt.

Is there any command to do that.? I do not like
to use sed or awk or any editors like vi.

Thoughts/idea are welcome.

Thanks and Regards,
carti
From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Wed Jul 27 13:11:13 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Wed Jul 27 13:10:34 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] viewing specific lines of file
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.58.0507270207220.655@chi.spunge.org>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0507271308460.13940-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

On Wed, 27 Jul 2005, carti wrote:

> I would like to view specific lines (range given in command line) of
> a file. Say for example, I want to view line numbers 27 to 39 of
> file file.txt.

Use Head and Tail

$ head -n 39 file.txt | tail -n 12 

39 - 27 = 12.

HTH :)
-- 
Bharathi S

Siddesh wrote:
>
> I had encountered a similiar problem in Mandrake
long ago.
>
> Make sure you configure KPPP with the ISP account
information in
> _both_ the root and normal user accounts. If you
configure the
> Internet account in root and launch it as a user,
chances are that it
> might not work (due to some weird user-friendliness
hacks in
> Mandr-ake/iva).
>

You might be right. I checked KPPP configuration as
user and found all the
coloumns in the
modem commands box were empty. So I launched KPPP as
root and copied all the
contents in the modem commands box. Now when I launch
KPPP as user it is 
working
fine. I did not have this problem when I was using
Mandrake 10.1.

Thanks for all those goa luggies who have replied.

R.Dhanagopal

Dear Mr. Balachander , Mr Mugunth raj and  friends,

I also faced a similiar problem with  my clients website
www.rscomptech.org. I was using windows platform as the operating
system. I was and I am using tata indicom telephone cdma service. I
was unable to access my client website  and the access pattern happend
to be discrete. some time i was able to access and some time i am not.
when i checked with the other isp Touchtel in a browsing center, the
webpage was browsing without any problem.

I nail down my problem with a tool 

www.megaproxy.com  through which in my machine i was able to browse
the troubled website and that the same cannot be browsed through my IE
browser and the same period (with a lag of 5 mins) and came to
conclusion that some malicious code was closing and opening the dns
door (for resolving) on and off discretely to the concerned web
site.other than
that i was unable to ping my website , but through megaproxy.com i can
able to browse my website through their dns support.

I see similarity in this issue, i would suggest you to back up your
data  and format your hard drive. I divorced windows and with linux
now living peacefully.

I am not running down to the conclusion saying that we both had the
same problem,you might check the same with www.megaproxy.com web site
and let me know.

I am a bit sure that this is not a propogational delay problem.

Let me know your response,

cheers

Thyagarajan.

but not me.in my opinion You cannot blame it on your isp (try with
dataone connection elsewhere at the same point of time ,try to ping 
it). So the question of Dns cache propogational delays is ruled out. I
understood the problem was at my end. So i reformatted my computer and
the problem was fixed. So at this point of time, i would request you

connection. The malicious code (which i faced) was targetting the web
site publishing system.

How about this one

sed -n 27,39p <filename>


Bharathi Subramanian wrote:

>On Wed, 27 Jul 2005, carti wrote:
>
>  
>
>>I would like to view specific lines (range given in command line) of
>>a file. Say for example, I want to view line numbers 27 to 39 of
>>file file.txt.
>>    
>>
>
>Use Head and Tail
>
>$ head -n 39 file.txt | tail -n 12 
>
>39 - 27 = 12.
>
>HTH :)
>

Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (APT-CACHE)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0507280942330.19301-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Mr Muthiah is released the G2 interface to Octave, which is used to 
get the graphs in different formats like PNG, JPEG, PS, EPS, X11...
URL: http://octave-gtk.sf.net/octave-g2/

One Day One Command 
===================

apt-cache -- Debian APT (Advanced Package Tool) package handling
             utility.

Summary:

apt-cache performs a variety of operations on APT's package cache.  
apt-cache does  not  manipulate the state of the system, but does
provide operations to search and generate interesting output from 
the package meta-data (/var/lib/apt/lists).

Examples:

$ apt-cache search xfree86 -- Show package info and descriptions for 
                              the search-string (xfree86).

$ apt-cache policy gcc -- Show version and priorities of the available 
                          Packages.

$ apt-cache show postgresql -- Show detailed description of postgresql
                               package.

$ apt-cache showpkg mozilla -- Show all kind of dependencies for the 
                               Mozilla package.

$ apt-cache depends mozilla -- List the packages needed by Mozilla.

$ apt-cache rdepends kde -- List all packages that needs KDE.

Read: man apt-cache

Debian Mirror in TamilNadu: http://ftp.iitm.ac.in/linux/
Debian Documentation  Link: http://www.debian.org/doc/
Debian CD Image Link : http://people.debian.org/cdimage/testing/

Bye :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Thu Jul 28 10:46:12 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Thu Jul 28 10:45:18 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] LJ Tech Tip
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0507271836050.13940-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Tech Tip from Linux Journal:

If you're formatting C code with "indent" and you have really awful
tricky parts that you want to leave with your own indenting, you can
make indent leave them alone by putting:

/* *INDENT-OFF* */  before each "special" chunk of code, and

/* *INDENT-ON* */   after it.

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
