From prem at songbirdtech.com  Thu Jul 28 00:26:26 2005
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Thu Jul 28 12:56:39 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: ilugc Digest, Vol 14, Issue 75
In-Reply-To: <20050728063002.440241DB265@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
References: <20050728063002.440241DB265@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <1134.61.247.255.57.1122535586.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

> we are using Cobalt Qube3 mail server, iam receiving
> junk /spam mails every day atleast a in 100's. when i
> receive this junk mails, some mails were bounce's
> back. So in this case our ISP were treating us as a
> spammers. how can I either stop these kinds of mails
> or how can i drop these mails, iam using
> sendmail(idont know the version). Can u people help
> me.
>
> Thanks,
>
> A.K Kannan

You will not receive bounced emails unless there is a machine on your
network sending out these emails in the first place. It seems to me that
you might have a trojaned machine on your network which is sending out
spam emails. Your best bet is to update virus signatures on all machines
on the network and run a full test to determine if there are trojans.

If this does not isolate the machine sending out the spam, then you can
setup a network sniffer which will pinpoint the machines on the network
sending out these packets. Once you have identified this machine, you can
resolve the problem by perhaps formatting and reinstalling the OS and
other software.

To answer your question about setting up Sendmail to make a copy of each
mail, yes - this is indeed possible. Please look at the Sendmail docs for
an explanation; one option is you can setup a default email id to which
all outgoing emails are copied automatically by your sendmail server - but
this does not in itself handle the case of documents leaving your network
without your permission because it is possible to use a separate SMTP
server other than your sendmail server to send out emails. Additionally,
documents can be sent over Yahoo! messenger, MSN and other IMs.

One point to Joe Steeve - you are not automatically guaranteed the right
to privacy on a corporate network. The computers you might use on your
corporate network are not considered your private space / private property
and what you do on those machines can be monitored and tracked. This
applies even to emails, your chat sessions, your browsing habits and so
on. This is true in the west and this is particularly true in India since
we don't have any strong privacy laws unlike in the West.

Regards,
Prem Kurian Philip
Songbird Technologies

It is unlikely that this is due to a malicious software installed on your
machine. It seems to me that your home machine is pointing to a DNS server
which has not yet resolved the domain to the IP address. I understand that
you are running Linux at home.

Do you have a DNS server installed and running on your machine and are you
using this as your primary DNS server? If so, please consider using your
ISP's dns server.

Regards,
Prem

From bvijay at midascomm.com  Fri Jul 29 07:27:41 2005
From: bvijay at midascomm.com (Vijay Kumar)
Date: Fri Jul 29 12:57:42 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Help- std library functions source code
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.58.0507290205360.31037@chi.spunge.org>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.58.0507290205360.31037@chi.spunge.org>
Message-ID: <m3iryujb8z.fsf@yogini.midascomm.com>

carti <carti@chi.spunge.org> writes:

> If I want to have a look at how std library functions
> are implemented(say for example source code of strcmp
> or printf or itoa) where I need to look at.
> 
> Is there any other way other than downloading the 30MB
> gcc source which includes other programming languages'
> sources too.

uclibc - http://www.uclibc.org/downloads/

  uClibc (aka ?Clibc/pronounced yew-see-lib-see) is a C library for
  developing embedded Linux systems. It is much smaller than the GNU C
  Library, but nearly all applications supported by glibc also work
  perfectly with uClibc. Porting applications from glibc to uClibc
  typically involves just recompiling the source code. uClibc even
  supports shared libraries and threading. It currently runs on
  standard Linux and MMU-less (also known as ?Clinux) systems with
  support for alpha, ARM, cris, i386, i960, h8300, m68k, mips/mipsel,
  PowerPC, SH, SPARC, and v850 processors.

newlib - ftp://sources.redhat.com/pub/newlib/index.html

  Newlib is a C library intended for use on embedded systems. It is a
  conglomeration of several library parts, all under free software
  licenses that make them easily usable on embedded products.


Vijay

-- 
Free the Code,
Free the User.

Fedora comes with yum pre-installed. It also has up2date. I generally
use to update. U can use
#yum update

up2date has GUI based interface which means just select check-boxes & click.

HTML pages do not "run". HTML is a text markup system. They are
rendered by the browser, and I expect all browsers currently render
HTML just fine.

Firefox does drag and drop etc. Go to http://www.google.com/ig in
Firefox, sign in and customise the page.

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Fri Jul 29 19:06:53 2005

Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (DPKG)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0507291601110.3132-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Mr Muthiah is released the G2 interface to Octave, which is used to 
get the graphs in different formats like PNG, JPEG, PS, EPS, X11...
URL: http://octave-gtk.sf.net/octave-g2/

One Day One Command 
===================

dpkg -- A medium-level package manager for Debian.

Summary:

dpkg is a medium-level tool to install, build, remove and manage
Debian packages. The primary and more user-friendly front-end for 
dpkg is dselect(8).

Examples:

$ dpkg -l vi* -- List packages matching given pattern.

$ dpkg -I vim.deb -- Show vim package information.

$ dpkg -c vim.deb -- List the vim package contents.

$ dpkg -S /usr/bin/gcc -- Show which pkg is installed gcc.

$ dpkg --print-avail vim emacs -- Display details about package, as 
                                  found in /var/lib/dpkg/available

# dpkg -i vim.deb -- Install the vim package.

# dpkg -r elvis -- Remove the package.

# dpkg-reconfigure xfree86 -- Reconfigure the X Package.

# aptitude -- Console interface to APT package management.

# synaptic -- GUI to APT package management.

Read: man dpkg, aptitude, synaptic

Debian Mirror in TamilNadu: http://ftp.iitm.ac.in/linux/

Bye :)

Bharathi S

From siva.ilugc at gmail.com  Sat Jul 30 09:14:37 2005
From: siva.ilugc at gmail.com (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Sat Jul 30 09:14:48 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT] DSL/Wireless
In-Reply-To: <d2a92d61050729055877dc47d1@mail.gmail.com>
References: <d2a92d61050729055877dc47d1@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <a8f990120507292044544b5d1d@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/29/05, Binand Sethumadhavan <binand@gmail.com> wrote:
> 
> 
> http://tinyurl.com/654h5
> 
> It works great with BT in UK and a couple of other guys I have tried
> it with; is anyone using it with any of the ISPs in Chennai? I am on
> Tata Indicom broadband in Chennai (earlier VSNL broadband, still
> earlier Dishnet DSL).
> 
  I would recommend using the ISP-supplied ADSL modem, and
getting a Linksys WRT54G instead for the WiFi/Routing portion.
The main advantage is that the Linksys has alternative Linux-based
images/routing distros available for customizing it.

>  Does anyone
> have any suggestions for a decent cheap linux-compatible ethernet card
> for this PC?
>
   I've been having great luck with used 3Com 3c905 and Intel 82557/8/9
cards available from electronic scrap dealers for ~Rs.100 each. Both can
deliver close to the rated 100 Mbps with minimal interrupt overhead on the
CPU. Avoid Realtek like the plague - that seems to be the only chipset
on new cards available locally, but the CPU overhead is too high for serious
routing applications, and it costs 4x the cards I referenced earlier. 

Early Realteks had a serious bug related to the use of an in-band non-
escaped data-pattern as some kind of state machine reset on the MAC (this
may have been fixed on the 8139c, but I'm taking no chances. Anybody
who designed that kind of crap would have left other undetected crap 
floating around as well.)

Stick with Intel 82557/8/9, DEC/Intel 2114x (Tulip), AMD PCnet or 3Com,
and you'll have no problems. Use Realtek as a last resort, and only on client
desktops.

-Siva
From lramp at iitm.ac.in  Sat Jul 30 09:37:59 2005
From: lramp at iitm.ac.in (L-RAMP)
Date: Sat Jul 30 09:38:06 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] re: DSL/Wireless
Message-ID: <1706.59.144.5.245.1122696479.squirrel@wmail.iitm.ac.in>

The ADSL Modem you have uses PPPoE. It should technically work with any
ISP that provides DSL over PPPoE. Touchtel for instance, does PPPoA and so
your gizmo won't work with their service (the modem part). I recently
bought a modem in the US that can handle PPPoA and worked without any
problem. Of course, you can just buy /rent a modem here and use this as a
router / FW. The router / FW of course are independent of service / IP
protocol and the like.

Rajeev

From skarra at gmail.com  Sat Jul 30 12:37:33 2005
From: skarra at gmail.com (Sriram Karra)
Date: Sat Jul 30 12:37:43 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT] Books on MIPS
In-Reply-To: <c2455504050729235463759f0@mail.gmail.com>
References: <c2455504050729235463759f0@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <3f986c6905073000074d370847@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/30/05, Shuveb Hussain <shuveb@gmail.com> wrote:

> Has anyone spotted a book on MIPS in any of the bookshops
> here(Chennai)?

The definitive book for embedded mips programming is Dominic
Sweetman's 'See MIPS Run'.  It is a brilliantly written book and is a
standard reference in many commercial embedded software shops.  I am
not sure if there is an Indian edition available... but I am sure
someone like Eswar or Landmark will be able to order the US edition
for you.  If you are a professional MIPS programmer, it's worth every
bit of its $40 price tag.

Apart from detailed info about the MIPS architecture, the book also
has very clear discussions about many general programming topics, like
compiler optimizations, portability, endian issues (which is the
clearest and most comprehensive treatment of the subject I have come
across anywhere) and such.

-Karra

> When I mentioned "subversion" as the option, they want
> to use cvs as they feel it is well proven, is much of
> standards like stuffs etc.,

Subversion is also proven - Mono, KDE, GCC have all gone the SVN way. 
SVN is five years old and quite stable. Check out the testimonials and
CVS comparison sections on subversion.tigris.org.

> 
> The problem is like this. Right now, there is a server
> (hp-ux)and around 10 developers are working on their codes
> currently in different directories. The problem is there
> is only one account/username shared by all the users and we
> cannot get individual account in the server for each and
> every person. I heard something like cvs will identify
> the commits based on the login name. If that is the case,
> in the above scenario there will be problem.
> 

With SVN you don't have to cache your auth info and can supply it when
executing a svn command.

> Is there any way to share the same account and still
> maintain code efficiently by different developers without
> any problem.
> 
> I have started reading documentation and started to lay
> my hands on cvs on unix.
> 

I have heard of some HP-UX specific issues with SVN - If after some
research you find that it's not serious, SVN would be a better choice.

> Since I have only worked on wincvs(by blindly checking in
> and check out wihtout knowing what is happening internally),
> that too 3 years ago, I dont know much.
> 
> Any suggestion from the experts are most welcome.
> 

ILUGC list is the best place place to get SVN advice - I suspect one
or two folks who work on SVN hang out here ;-)

Ramaswamy

From base16 at gmail.com  Sat Jul 30 20:44:31 2005
From: base16 at gmail.com (Arvind Kalyan)
Date: Mon Aug  1 00:04:11 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] xine problem
In-Reply-To: <20050729095056.25127.qmail@web31005.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
References: <20050729095056.25127.qmail@web31005.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <90c25f270507300814198b0948@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/29/05, babu jayapaul <babu_jayapaul@yahoo.com> wrote:

> When I start to play any VCD/PIC in xine, The X window
> is restart and comes to login screen.

Using bash? Try this:

ulimit -c 253625424
xine 2> Xine.err

Now after the X restart, see if you have a file called core[.*] and
also see `less Xine.err` content.

Try debugging with that, using gdb.

If no success kindly get back with what you saw there. i.e., send the
Xine.err content and also the output of : $ gdb `which xine` coreFile
, then type 'bt' send us that.


Also tell me this:
1. Have you had success earlier?
2. Does this happen only for a particular (or a set of) video files?
3. Do you see /etc/X11/XvMCConfig file? If yes, what is inside it?
4. What is your kernel and DRM version?
5. You sure you have the necessary codecs for that DVD/VCD/whatever installed?

Thanks and regards,

-- 
Arvind Kalyan
http://www.devforge.net/~arv
